## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration–time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A(t), which is the standard formulation of reaction kinetics as an ODE. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, saturation/inhibition) and possibly explicitly on t (time-varying conditions or deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or saturated catalyst; constant-rate depletion)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A+A kinetics)
- n-th order (power-law) decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order)
- Mixed source–sink (CSTR/production+decay): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant generation with first-order loss)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (reversible lumped): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 - A) (rate proportional to A and remaining capacity/reactant)
- Inhibition (rational rate law): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (self-inhibition, crowding, or limited active sites)
- Strong inhibition / poisoning: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturating inhibition with characteristic concentration c1)
- Time-varying first-order (e.g., catalyst deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decays over time)
- Linear time drift in rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (slowly changing conditions during the run)
- Oscillatory forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodic temperature/illumination/flow modulation)
- Induction/activation term (smooth start): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps up from 0 due to activation/mixing)
- Parallel pathways lumped into polynomial: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular loss routes)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- dA_dt proportional to A (linear in A) indicates first-order kinetics; semi-log A(t) would be approximately linear in time.
- dA_dt proportional to A**2 indicates bimolecular/self-reaction behavior; 1/A vs t tends to be approximately linear.
- A-independent dA_dt (constant) suggests zero-order kinetics (surface saturation, constant photon flux, or mass-transfer-limited regime).
- Presence of an additive term (e.g., c0 - c1*A) indicates feed/production or dilution plus reaction (common in reactors with inflow/outflow).
- A shifted by a constant (A - c1) indicates relaxation toward a steady/equilibrium concentration c1 (net forward and reverse lumped).
- Rational forms like A/(1+c*A) indicate saturation/inhibition or finite active-site availability; rate increases at low A and flattens at high A.
- Factors like exp(-c*t) multiplying the rate indicate time-dependent rate constants (catalyst deactivation, changing temperature, aging).
- Sin(c*t) modulation indicates periodically forced kinetics (light-driven reactions, temperature cycling, oscillatory feed).
- Terms like A*(c1-A) imply self-amplifying/limited-capacity dynamics (autocatalysis with depletion of a limiting resource or approach to a cap).

1. `c_a * A^(1/3)` (cube root of A)
2. `c_b * A^2` (quadratic in A)
3. `c_c * A * exp(c_d * t)` (A times exponential decay in t)

The key basis functions are: **A^(1/3)**, **A^2**, and **A*exp(k*t)**.

Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce exactly these three basis functions.

**Candidates with polynomial terms (A^2, A, constant) plus A*exp(ct):**

Many candidates (1, 3, 4, 6-17, 20-21, 23-25, 30, 34, 38, 43) have terms like A^2, A*exp(ct), A, and constants, but lack A^(1/3). They might have rational terms like A*c/(A*c+c) or c/(A+c), but these cannot produce A^(1/3). These are **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with Abs(A) terms (18, 19, 26, 28, 31, 35, 40, 42, 44-50):**

Under domain A ≥ 0, |A| = A. So A*c*|A| = c*A^2. Some candidates have |A|^c4 which could give A^(1/3) if c4=1/3.

- **Candidate 45:** `A + c0 + c1*|A| + c2*exp(c3*t)*|A|^c4`. With A≥0: `A + c0 + c1*A + c2*exp(c3*t)*A^c4`. This gives terms: A (linear), constant, A (linear), A^c4 * exp(c3*t). The exp term is coupled with A^c4, but GT needs A*exp(kt) and A^(1/3) separately. Cannot decouple. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 49:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)*|A|^c4`. Same issue - exp coupled with A^c4. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 18:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*|A| + A*c4 + c5`. With A≥0: c3*A^2 + c1*A*exp(c2*t) + (c0+c4)*A + c5. Has A^2 and A*exp, but no A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 50:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5*|A| + c6`. = c5*A^2 + (c0)*A + c1*A*exp(c2*t) + c3*A*exp(c4*t) + c6. Set c3=0: A^2 + A*exp + A + const. No A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with log terms (28, 35):** log(A*c+1) ≠ A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with exp(A*c) terms (5, 8, 14, 22, 27, 29, 32, 36, 37, 39):** exp(A*c) with c=0 gives constant 1, reducing to polynomial. Check if remaining terms can give A^(1/3). None can. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 2, 33:** These have A^(1/3) and A^(4/3) denominators. Let me check Candidate 2. The denominator is A^(4/3)+A^(1/3) = A^(1/3)(A+1). Simplifying terms: A^(10/3)/(A^(1/3)(A+1)) = A^3/(A+1) = A^2 - A + 1 - 1/(A+1). This introduces 1/(A+1) which can't produce A^(1/3). Also has exp(A*c) and log terms. Too complex and wrong basis. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 40, 42, 44:** Have A^c or (A*c+1)^c which could give A^(1/3), but also have |A|^c*exp(ct) coupling. In Candidate 40: `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*|A|/(c5+|A|) + c6*exp(c7*t)*|A|^c8`. Set c4=0, c1=1/3, c8=1: gives A^(1/3) + A*exp(kt) + A + const. No A^2. **NO MATCH**.

After thorough analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce exactly the three basis functions A^(1/3), A^2, and A*exp(kt).

Matched candidate IDs: []

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
